From Markus Grassl June 2007.

Grassl found 95 erroneous entries in my (Warren Smith's) May 2007 table of generator polynomials
for BCH codes.  This is a fairly small fraction of Smith's table but clearly indicates
there is a bug in Smith's program, just a bug that gets activated fairly rarely, making it
hard to find(?).  There's a lot of underlying unchecked stuff in Smith's
program such as tables of primitive polynomials, which could contain bugs.
MAGMA probably is a lot less buggy in that respect.

Grassl computed BCH-code generator polynomials for all odd lengths up to 513
using MAGMA.  Furthermore, Grassl spent SOME time on computing the code's minimum
distance - not enough to always succeed, but sometimes enough.
That also served as a good sanity check on the BCH code computation.
If there is an entry of the form [n,k,d] in Grassl's list, then
d is the true minimum distance.  For entries [n,k,>=d], a lower bound
on the minimum distance is given which is not yet known to be the true
minimum distance.  However, this lower bound might be higher than the BCH bound.

Note, for narrow sense binary BCH codes (which these are) the min dist
is known always to be ODD.  Therefore if Grassl's distance lower bound
is even, you can improve it by adding 1.

This data was computed by Grassl from scratch
and does not incorporate knowledge from his code database.
=============
